    <li> I am totally sold on this product. No more sulfate shampoos for me. I love how my hair feels after washing with this conditioning cleanser. My hair is fine, and thin, and this product works well for me.</li>
    <li> I don&#x27;t know quite how they did it, but they managed to create a product that leaves your scalp greasy and your hair stripped of all moisture. My hair is very fine and wavy-curly, requires gentle cleansing and generous conditioning / protection to be manageable, and to let the natural curl set when air dried. This product sells as an alternative to harsh shampoos and thick conditioners, but was harsher than anything I&#x27;ve ever used on my hair (and I once used dishwashing liquid while camping). I followed the instructions to the letter, and the result was a tangled unmanageable head of frizzy hair with an oddly matted / grimy scalp. I even gave it more than one shot, read other reviews, used more product and so on. The result was always the same: an unhappy head of hair that looked like blonde cotton candy. Plus it REEKS! Although some might find the scent pleasing, for me it was like being punched in the nose with grandma&#x27;s sachet. It may work well on some other type of hair, but for baby-fine curls, this product is a disaster.</li>
    <li> The best cleansing conditioner out there hands down ! Smells amazing and there are enough suds that hair feels clean but no harsh SLS! I  have fine hair and I find that I have to wash less often after using this for awhile! On off days I use a little &amp;#34;skinny skinny &amp;#34; brand organic dry shampoo powder (buy some its the best!) and that&#x27;s all I need to skip a day. They ONLY thing I hate about this is the small size of the bottle and the pump is just stupid. Only a tiny amount comes out I have to pump it 20 times to get enough! Next time I might actually transfer it to another pump bottle that works better and add a little water . You have to add water anyway when you try to later it.... Other than that I would give it 10 stars!</li>
    <li> I love this cleansing conditioner! It smells amazing and the scent lasts for days. I too bought this because Wen is too expensive, I like this better so it&#x27;s a win, win. It leaves my hair soft and silky and the style really holds without using a styling product. The bonus is it doesn&#x27;t weigh my hair down and it doesn&#x27;t get oily as fast either, I can actually go 3 days between shampoos instead of my usual 2. My only complaint is the bottle isn&#x27;t big enough and the pump is very short, it takes a lot of pumping to lather your hair. Will I buy this again or recommend it to others...I most definitely will!</li>
    <li> I have been a long time user of the Deva products. This is a nice option that is much less expensive. I always find my hair does best when I switch up my products, so I like having another option aside from the Deva. Given the price, there is no reason not to try it.</li>

    <li> This is great and it smells wonderful, my hair is so wonderfully revived, soft, and touchable!</li>
    <li> I&#x27;m writing this review the actual day I bought this product &amp; tried it. I recently starting swimming for the summer &amp; my usual shampoo &amp; conditioner wasn&#x27;t cutting it anymore. I needed more hydration, so I decided to try some of these cleansing conditioners out of curiosity. I haven&#x27;t tried WEN, simply because I&#x27;m not willing to pay tons of money on a bottle that will last less than a month so I started looking into other options. First I tried Salon Grafix (which my local supermarket now carries) for about $8.00 for 12oz. Not too bad considering. I used it for several days in a row &amp; it&#x27;s pretty good. Rinses easily &amp; has next to no noticeable smell at all (which is nice). It doesn&#x27;t lather at all though &amp; you feel like you&#x27;re putting straight conditioner on top of dirty hair-which feels a bit creepy in the shower quite honestly. However, it doesn&#x27;t leave your hair greasy, just soft &amp; clean. I assume this is similar to WEN. THEN out of curiosity I decided to try this Loreal version because the local drug store caries it &amp; it is also inexpensive-though the bottle is only 8oz. When you&#x27;re looking at ounces, you get less with Loreal, however it seems you don&#x27;t need to use quite as much on your hair (at least I didn&#x27;t). Maybe a couple pumps less. Loreal cleansing conditioner seems to have much more oils in it, as I noticed it really detangled my long (to my waist) hair better than the other brand did. I liked that aspect about it-it&#x27;s very conditioning. HOWEVER, the smell is JUST SOOOOOO STRONG!!! I read various reviews on it beforehand, &amp; many people mentioned the horrible smell, yet a few people liked it, so I figured I would try it myself &amp; judge. The smell is WAAAY TOO MUCH! One person mentioned it smells like sugar cookies, &amp; yes it does to an extent, but it has that really stong \\&quot;old lady\\&quot; smell as well. Imagine perfumed baby powder mixed with a hint of vanilla &amp; that&#x27;s about it. The smell lasts on your hair LONG after the shower &amp; for those sensitive to scent you WILL NOT LIKE THIS! I can see how it gave one person a headache easily. It almost did me as well + it made my scalp a little itchy too from too much fragrance. My boyfriend too could smell it at least a foot away from me. Geeze! I really don&#x27;t know why they only offer 1 scent (&amp; not a very good one at that)! Not everyone wants to smell like perfumey food. A cucumber mint would be better, or lavender, or ginger, just something more refreshing. After my hair dried, the smell persisted &amp; was so strong that I could no longer stand it. It&#x27;s just plan GROSS &amp; I decided to re-wash my hair w/my old shampoo &amp; conditioner to get it out. I didn&#x27;t want to go to bed w/that smell &amp; have it on my pillow case, etc. I couldn&#x27;t believe it, but after trying to wash it out I could STILL SMELL IT in my hair &amp; this is after ONE USE PEOPLE!!!! Now that&#x27;s SCARY! For a product to be this perfumey is plain creepy &amp; I am returning it ASAP to the store. I will never buy this stuff again! How anyone can like it is beyond me. It leaves your hair feeling coated w/a film too. YUCK!!! Possibly if used regularly you might get a buildup on your hair &amp; it could get greasy. Oh well, back to Salon Grafix for me. For the record, I have not tried the RENpure brand yet. That might be my next experiment just to see how it is.</li>
    <li> My first impression of this product was to laugh at how little comes out of the bottle with each pump. You have to pump about 20 times to get enough to cleanse short hair.  The smell is fairly strong -- an artificial, plastic smell that is covered up partially by sweet vanilla tones. Luckily, the smell faded once my hair was dry. I did notice my hair felt very soft later in the day.  But overall, I prefer [[ASIN:B00641UCY8 As I Am Coconut Cowash Cleansing Conditioner, 16 Ounce]], which is another economical cleansing conditioner.</li>

    <li> Great for color treated hair. Smells good too and who doesn&#x27;t like great smelling hair.</li>
    <li> I saw this on the Today Show over the holidays and have been looking for it in my drugstore ever since.  I have been a fan of sulfate-free products for years because I color my hair and everytime I shampoo with nonsulfate free I imagine the color just washing off my head.  Anyway, I already use Ever Pure so am familiar  with and like Loreal products (use Feria for color).  I love this product.  They thing that most intrigued me was saving time by combining shampoo and conditioner.  Every shampoo with built-in conditioner that I have previously tried is too much shampoo and not enough conditioner.  I have really think hair so i am left with a lot of tangles.  This is not that at all.  Went on like a conditioner but also cleaned.  This is a low-poo so it will not lather up like you are used to with sulfate shampoo. OK so enough rambling.......here&#x27;s how to use it&lt;br /&gt;1. Remember, this is a product that does NOT lather. Think of it as using as using a moisturising cream cleanser for your hair (much as you might use for your face) vs using a harsh, drying soap (i.e. traditional latering shampoo)..it&#x27;s the same concept, and once you start with this type of product, you will be so pleased with the results.&lt;br /&gt;2. Make sure your hair is throughly wet. The only bad thing about this product is the pump...it dispenses WAY too little product per pump. Based on the thickness and length of your hair, you may need as little as 5 pumps, or, if you have long, thick wavy hair like mine that goes down to your mid back, you may need 12-20. I use about 12- 15...&lt;br /&gt;3. Start by working the product into and all the way around your scalp, moving the product down to the ends. Its a bit thicker than shampoo, of course, and it will take some getting used to, but keep working at it&lt;br /&gt;4. take as many pumps as you like to coat the ends of your hair. You will find as you get used to using this that when you do the final rinse, the product will run down into the ends of your hair cleaning and softening it, so this part you may not even want to do.&lt;br /&gt;5. take a few minutes and get on with your shower, shave, etc....&lt;br /&gt;6 after at least 3 minutes, add water to the scalp and hair, and continue to work it in a bit, (you will find this part easier than when you first applied it) then start to rinse.&lt;br /&gt;7. Rinse throughly....rinse!!&lt;br /&gt;8. Finish with a light conditioner if you wish. Fine haired, normal or un damaged textured people might skip this part all together....I personally use a light conditioner always.&lt;br /&gt;9. Dry your hair and style&lt;br /&gt;10.     <li> This crme cleanser is very effective with keeping my hair soft, shiny and manageable.  It is not regular shampoo, so you might need some practice (like you would with Wen), in order to really use it the right way.  I flip my head over and let the water run on the back of my head and really saturate my hair (I find this is the best way for me to use this product).  Next, I put a few pumps (you will figure out how much you need eventually) in my hand and start with the first section (the front of my head).  I gently massage the cleanser on my scalp until a low lather develops.  Then I continue this method throughout my whole head.  I also add a few splashes of water to create an effective lather.  If you don&#x27;t use enough water then it will not work correctly.  After I have a nice low lather, I finger comb or use a wide tooth comb to distribute the product to the rest of my hair.  Then I clip my hair up and let it sit while I wash my body.  This type of cleanser does take work, but once you get the hang of it, you will be very satisfied with the results.  I&#x27;m sure YouTube has instructional videos if you are unsure of how to apply the product.  It is very similar to Wen, although I find that Wen is the best cleanser for hair EVER, although very expensive!  This is a close second!  I have long fine hair and a very oily scalp (I have to wash my hair everyday or else I have a grease slick!) and this product does not leave my hair greasy.  My ends are dry too when I use traditional shampoos, but when I use this cleanser, my ends blow out so nice and my hair doesn&#x27;t separate as much or look straggly.  Enjoy!</li>

SCENT&lt;br /&gt;Loreal: I know a lot of people in the reviews complained about the scent.  Honestly, I did not notice that the scent was either good or bad.  It did not bother me either way.  HOWEVER, my 11 year old daughter, had to use the bathroom when I was using the product and asked me , &amp;#34;What smells like rotten eggs?&amp;#34;, and she insisted that my hair smelled bad after I had blow dried it, even though I could not smell it. THE PRODUCT DIFFERENCES&lt;br /&gt;It is very important to note that Loreal is a LOW LATHER cleansing conditioner, but Wen is a NO LATHER cleansing conditioner.  They are BOTH cleansing conditioner, but there is a big difference.  When I used Wen, I did not feel like I was putting shampoo on my hair.  There was no lather, no pull on my hair, nofriction.  I was stunned that I did not lose ANY (not 1) hair when I used Wen, but that my hair still felt clean and deep conditioned at the same time.  When I first put the Loreal cleansing conditioner into my hands, it felt like conditioner, like Wen.  But when you put it in your hair and work it in, you see that there are suds.  I was very disappointed when this happened.  After I towed dried, I could barely comb through my hair and had to use my daughter&#x27;s detangler.  When using both products, I followed through with the rest of my hair care routine as usual, however when using the Loreal cleansing conditioner, after blow drying, my hair felt very dry and straw-like, as if I hadn&#x27;t conditioned at all.  I had to add extra Moroccan oil to my hair, but it still did not look or feel right.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. I think that this product is probably a good shampoo, and I would feel okay using it as a shampoo if followed by my Organix Moroccan Oil deep conditioner. It very well could be my hair (I&#x27;ve tried other alternative/\\&quot;no shampoo\\&quot; routes with little success), so if you have very thick, dry hair, this might be for you. Also, I have pretty manageable hair to begin with, so I&#x27;m just going back to regular shampoo and a strong conditioner for my ends.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;**Original Post with 4-star review**&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve been using this product for about 2 months now, and I&#x27;m a fan. Am I a rabid fan? No, but I also have pretty manageable, straight, happy hair, so I haven&#x27;t noticed any life-altering changes like others have mentioned.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I started using this product because I wanted to use so something less harsh on my hair, and potentially find a better oil/ moisture balance for my poor, greasy scalp. I have very fine, thin, blondish hair, but lots of it. I&#x27;ve always been the kind of person who needs to wash my hair every day or else I look like a greaseball. Without dry shampoo (a lifesaver) I&#x27;d start getting piece-y hair 24 hours post-wash.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The first several times I used this product, it felt like I could not rinse it all out for the life of me. I&#x27;d massage it in my scalp, leave it in to do its magic, and rinse, rinse, rinse to no avail. When my hair was dry, there were always patches (usually at the nape of neck or somewhere in the back of my head) that felt disgusting and greasy. I tried using more product as recommended, something like 8-10 pumps, but that didn&#x27;t work either.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THen someone on here recommended that you NOT LEAVE the product in your hair in the shower. This has worked magic for me. I use 3-4 pumps to quickly lather as much as I can at the top, sides/back and nape of thehead, and rinse immediately. I then use 4-5 more pumps for another quick, more thorough lather and rinse. I do all of this at the beginning of my shower to let the water run over my hair for extra measure. Make sure to get a lather, as I&#x27;ve found that is key. It&#x27;s a very low lather product, but you do get a little bit while you get a quick arm workout. I personally finish off with a vinegar rinse (one part white vinegar to about three parts water, plus a couple drops of essential oil), which I find helpful.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One caveat: none of this may work for you if you live someplace with very hard water. I vacationed in Santa Fe this Christmas, and this stuff never wanted to rinse out of my hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for the smell, I don&#x27;t care for it. It&#x27;s very sweetly vanilla-ish. I usually like sweet floral smells (I currently wear Gucci Glamorous Magnolia), and this is just not my favorite. Good thing the scent doesn&#x27;t stay in my hair, which might be due to the vinegar rinse ;)</li>

I&#x27;ve wanted to convert to using a cleansing conditioner, anyhow. I tried it once and wasn&#x27;t impressed. My hair felt kind of dry and a little tangled. I couldn&#x27;t really figure out why.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oh, except this has rubbing alcohol in it. \\&quot;Isopropyl alcohol\\&quot; is indeed on its ingredient list.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why? There is no reason. Rubbing alcohol is not good for your hair or scalp in any sense of the word. It is astringent and drying. I assume this may be included as part of the \\&quot;cleansing,\\&quot; but that&#x27;s just silly. Also, behentrimonium chloride, a cleanser, is a known and accepted skin irritant.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I know I sound pretty angry, but honestly, I am. There&#x27;s only one hair product requiring alcohol, and that&#x27;s hairspray. [[ASIN:B001DJ2USM L&#x27;Oreal Paris Elnett Satin Hairspray, Extra Strong Hold, 11 Ounce]] is a good example. I&#x27;ll admit that I like to use it, the few times a year I go for hairspray. Alcohol dissolves after a while, allowing for a fine, misting application. They make alcohol-free hairsprays, but due to their pump application, they often have a more uneven application. I understand its use in hairspray. I certainly don&#x27;t understand its use in \\&quot;conditioner.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oh, and the scent is intolerably strong. It&#x27;s like shoving bits of sugar cookies and baby powder up your nose.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Forget it, L&#x27;Oreal. Some tips for using this cleansing conditioner are:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Use a clarifying or regular shampoo first if your hair is full of styling product (In my experience, the cleansing conditioner is not strong enough to take these products out of your hair)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Make sure you really soak your hair in water before you apply the product (Water helps the product to lather up a bit)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Find out what number of pumps work best for you (If  you have short hair, 8-10 pumps may be enough. I need about 16-18 pumps for my hair, but it is thick and about 5 inches past my shoulders).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Once the product is lathered, I leave it on for a minute or two and then add a splash of water.
